JDBC connection: Max Number of Connections: 0
–∏ –ø–µ—Ä–µ—Å–æ–∑–¥–∞–≤–∞—Ç—å VU, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–π –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑—É–µ—Ç –ø–æ–¥–∫–ª—é—á–µ–Ω–∏–µ

https://jmeter.apache.org/usermanual/component_reference.html#JDBC_Connection_Configuration

Maximum number of connections allowed in the pool. In most cases, set this to zero (0). This means that each thread will get its own pool with a single connection in it, i.e. the connections are not shared between threads.
If you really want to use shared pooling (why?), then set the max count to the same as the number of threads to ensure threads don't wait on each other.

Vitaliy Kudryashov
In reply to this message 
You might think that memory utilization is easily tracked with container_memory_usage_bytes, however, this metric also includes cached (think filesystem cache) items that can be evicted under memory pressure. The better metric is container_memory_working_set_bytes as this is what the OOM killer is watching for.
